- **`operatorBetweenFilters` filter execution path (MISS-002).** Rationale: BUG-001 closed the orchestrator wiring; the actual `SearchService.buildRefinementFilters` consistency issue is Sprint 4 backlog per `CLAUDE.md`. Same shape as MISS-001 — D5's validation can warn "OR semantics may not apply consistently across filter groups" until the execution path lands.
- **In-product admin onboarding tour / guided first-time-config wizard.** Rationale: D11's docs links + D9's pre-flight tab cover the same intent at lower implementation cost. A guided tour adds runtime overlay management + per-step skip/recall persistence that exceeds the audience-profile bar at v1.0.
- **Admin theming / per-context color palette overrides.** Rationale: spec §3 and T1 Out of Scope item ("Layout-A/B testing or admin theming UI") explicitly reject this — admins use SharePoint section themes. Repeating the rejection here so it doesn't accrete in T4 reviews.
- **Telemetry on property pane usage (which fields admins touch most).** Rationale: spec §4.4 Foundations owns the broader telemetry decision. Admin-pane telemetry is a meaningful T4 input but cannot ship before the opt-in / tenant-config telemetry plumbing exists. v1.1 candidate.
- **Multi-tenant / multi-environment property pane profiles (e.g. dev / staging / prod overrides per environment).** Rationale: out of audience-profile scope ("self-serve any tenant"). Profile management at the SPFx property pane layer would require a per-environment store + import/export round-trip; admins managing environments today use SPPKG packaging or PnP provisioning templates. Defer.
- **Visual property pane editor (drag-and-drop layout designer instead of typed property pane).** Rationale: PnP Modern Search v4 has none; SP Search has none; not a parity-driven gap. The typed property pane is the correct shape for SPFx; a visual editor is a different product. Reject.
- **Bundled SPFx Property Pane page templates (e.g. "Documents page", "People page" as one-click property pane preset profiles).** Rationale: D12 ships scenario preset propagation across web parts which covers the same intent at smaller scope; a separate page-template registry would duplicate that work. v1.1 candidate if D12's per-web-part suggestion path proves insufficient.



### T5. Observable & Diagnosable

#### Current state

T5 is the differentiator that proves SP Search isn't a black box on the day a user files a ticket. Per spec §4.3, the track explicitly distinguishes two categories that are kept separate everywhere in this section: **(A) Local diagnostics** — admin/user-visible debug state, support bundle, recent network/search calls, config snapshot, with no external send; and **(B) Telemetry** — optional aggregate signals, opt-in only, never captures query text, user identity, result titles, URLs, tenant names, or list item content. Today the surface is asymmetric: local diagnostics has a real (but partial) implementation; telemetry has zero implementation and no opt-in plumbing. Both categories ship behind the same admission gate (`?debug=1` URL parameter) but they belong to different audiences (admins for telemetry-aggregate, support engineers for local), and the section structure reflects that.

The actual T5 surface, by file:

**(A) Local diagnostics — what exists today.**

- **DebugCollector singleton.** `src/libraries/spSearchStore/debug/DebugCollector.ts:1-101` is a window-keyed singleton (`__sp_search_debug_collector__` at `:3`) that collects `IDebugEvent[]` (capped at `MAX_EVENTS = 200` at `:4, 59-61`), a single `lastQuery: IQueryDebugInfo | undefined` slot (`:11, 65-70`), a `webPartConfigs: Map<string, IWebPartDebugConfig>` (`:12, 72-82`), and a listener set for subscribers (`:14, 96-100`). All collection methods short-circuit on `!isActive()` (`:50, 66, 73`); `isActive()` is computed once from `window.location.search.indexOf('debug=1') >= 0` (`:39-46`). Six event types: `SEARCH | FILTER | VERTICAL | URL | ERROR | INIT` (`IDebugTypes.ts:1`).
- **DebugCollector wiring across the codebase.** `grep -rn 'DebugCollector' src` returns 22 hits across 11 files. Every web part calls `DebugCollector.registerWebPart` in `onInit` (Box `:161`, Filters `:143`, Verticals `:111`, Results `:296`, Manager `:156`, Admin Manager `:19`). Orchestrator emits `setLastQuery` twice per search (`SearchOrchestrator.ts:313-329` pre-execute, `:411-441` post-execute), `logEvent('SEARCH')` once per success (`:442-448`), `logEvent('ERROR')` once per failure (`:498-503`). URL middleware emits `logEvent('URL')` for push (`urlSyncMiddleware.ts:599`) and popstate (`:759`). Slices emit `logEvent('FILTER')` on set/remove/clearAll (`filterSlice.ts:137, 146, 151`) and `logEvent('VERTICAL')` on switch (`verticalSlice.ts:12`). `INIT` is auto-emitted from `registerWebPart` (`DebugCollector.ts:80`).
- **DebugFab + DebugPanel UI.** `src/webparts/spSearchResults/components/DebugFab.tsx:1-35` (a 35-line FAB with bug icon + 5-second-error pulse) and `DebugPanel.tsx:1-458` (a 458-line bottom-drag-to-resize panel with **four tabs: Query / State / Config / Log** at `:382-387`). Tab payloads: Query renders `kql`, `queryTemplate`, `resultSourceId`, `providerId`, `timing` (with green/yellow/red <500/<2000/≥2000ms classification at `:17-21`), `results count`, `refinementFilters`, `refiners`, `error`, `request` JSON tree, `response` JSON tree (`:103-191`); State renders 6-slice live snapshot with 2-second highlight on changed keys (`:193-278`); Config renders per-web-part `properties` from `webPartConfigs` (`:280-312`); Log renders the 200-event ring buffer with per-type filter checkboxes (`:316-371`).
- **Where DebugFab is mounted.** `grep -rn 'DebugFab\|DebugPanel' src` confirms the FAB and panel are rendered **only by `SpSearchResults.tsx:71-75, 839-848`**. The other five web parts (Box, Filters, Verticals, Manager, Admin Manager) feed events into `DebugCollector` via `registerWebPart` but render no FAB and no panel. A page that hosts Box + Filters + Verticals but no Results web part has no in-product debug surface, even on `?debug=1`.
- **Error surfacing patterns — three styles, no shared abstraction.** `grep -rn 'MessageBar' src/webparts | grep -v test | wc -l` returns 5+ web parts and 30+ call sites using Fluent `MessageBar` (e.g., `ZeroResultsPanel.tsx:150-155`, `CoverageStatsSection.tsx:45`, `SavedSearchList.tsx:459-461`, `ShareSearchDialog.tsx:301-327`, `SearchInsightsPanel.tsx:6`, `SpSearchResults.tsx:716-720, 738-741`). One ad-hoc toast lives in `DataGridContent.tsx:509, 1053-1060` (custom `<div>` portal with `role="status" aria-live="polite"`, copy-URL confirmation only). Inline renders are scattered — `EmptyState` at `SpSearchResults.tsx:402-444` for zero results; `error` strings written into `state.error` and rendered conditionally inline; `ErrorBoundary` from spfx-toolkit wraps the root tree in five web parts (`SpSearchBox.tsx:924-926`, `SpSearchVerticals.tsx:269-275`, `SpSearchManager.tsx:996-998`, `SpSearchResults.tsx:713`, plus a custom `DataGridRenderErrorBoundary` at `DataGridLayout.tsx:50-115` that falls back to List layout). No `Toast` adoption from spfx-toolkit (`grep -rn 'spfx-toolkit/lib/components/Toast' src` returns 0 hits) despite CLAUDE.md listing `Toast / ToastProvider` as a "Component used" for "Save/share/export notifications" — gap between docs and code.
- **"Why no results" treatment today.** `EmptyState` (`SpSearchResults.tsx:402-444`) renders four context-aware copy variants based on `(queryText, hasActiveFilters)` and offers two recovery affordances ("Clear all filters" + "Start over"). Recovery is generic — same copy regardless of WHY the result set is empty. The orchestrator knows several failure modes the empty state never surfaces: filter values producing zero rows (could surface "removing the FileType filter would return N results"); a `queryTemplate` token resolving to a wrong scope (no diagnostic); a `dataProviderId` typo silently routed to the fallback provider (T3 surface); a managed-property typo in a refiner producing an empty bucket (T4 surface). Only `querySuggestion` from the search response surfaces ("Did you mean…" via `setQuerySuggestion` at `SearchOrchestrator.ts:403` rendered at `SpSearchResults.tsx:767-779`). A user staring at "No results for 'Q4 budget'" has no diagnostic path beyond clearing filters or starting over.
- **Network / recent-call capture.** `IDebugTypes.ts:25-27` has a single `request` slot and a single `response` slot on the `lastQuery` record — only the **most recent search query** is preserved with full payload. Vertical-count queries (`SearchOrchestrator.ts:582`), base-refiner queries (`:344-360`), coverage stats queries (`CoverageStatsService.ts:29-60`), Search Manager service calls to `SearchSavedQueries` / `SearchHistory` / `SearchCollections` lists (~30+ PnPjs calls in `SearchManagerService.ts`), and Graph calls to `/communications/presences` (`GraphSearchProvider.ts`) are NOT captured by the DebugCollector at all. No network tab in DebugPanel; no per-call timing breakdown; no payload size tracking; no per-provider call count.
- **Errors tab.** No dedicated Errors tab. ERROR events live in the same Log tab ring buffer with the other five types and are filtered by toggling the ERROR checkbox at `DebugPanel.tsx:316, 344-355`. `error.stack` is captured in the event payload at `SearchOrchestrator.ts:498-503` but the Log tab only renders `JSON.stringify(event.data)` inline (`DebugPanel.tsx:363`) — no stack-trace formatting, no source-mapping, no group-by-error-type aggregation.
- **Console-log discipline (PII review).** `grep -rn 'console\.\(log\|info\|warn\|error\|debug\)' src/libraries src/webparts | wc -l` returns 40 hits across the source tree. `state.queryText || '*'` is written to `console.log` four times in `SearchOrchestrator.ts:293, 463, 493, 501` — at "First search starting", "Search complete" (debug level), "Search failed" (error level), and inside the `DebugCollector.logEvent('ERROR', { query: state.queryText })` payload. The query text is the most user-identifying free-text field in the product; on a tenant where users search for sensitive terms (employee names, internal project codes, settlement amounts, performance reviews), the browser console retains those strings indefinitely and they are visible to anyone the user shares a screen with. SearchManagerService logs `[SP Search] loadSavedSearches: loaded N items` (`:467, 565, 617, 1117`) and similar — non-PII counts, but no rate-limit or production-mode gate. No central log shim with severity / namespace / production filter.
- **Coverage Stats + Admin Dashboard analytics.** `CoverageStatsService.ts:1-244` queries `SearchAggregations` for itemCount / newest-oldest dates / fileTypes / actualSites buckets per coverage-profile URL. Wired into the `AdminDashboard.tsx` Coverage tab (rendered at `AdminDashboard.tsx:206`, with `CoverageStatsSection` as the component file). `QualityMetricsSection` (rendered at `AdminDashboard.tsx:227`), `ZeroResultsPanel` (rendered at `AdminDashboard.tsx:248`; component file is 249 lines), and `SearchInsightsPanel` (rendered at `AdminDashboard.tsx:268`; component file is 559 lines) round out the four-panel dashboard (T4.D7 owns the depth gaps — UX-005/006/007). The dashboard runs on aggregate data from `SearchHistory` (per-user-readable per Data Rule #1) PLUS cross-user reads via `loadAllHistoryForInsights` and `loadZeroResultQueries` (admin-gated). For T5 the relevant gap is **support-engineer-facing diagnostics** versus admin-facing analytics: dashboard answers "is the deployment healthy?" but does not answer "why did THIS user's last query fail?".

**(B) Telemetry — what exists today.**

- **Nothing.** `grep -rn 'telemetry\|analytics\|appInsights\|fetch.*\.com\|sendBeacon\|navigator\.sendBeacon' src` returns 0 results across the source tree (matches in code are unrelated — `track` referring to user-visible click tracking written to the local `SearchHistory` list, not telemetry). No opt-in toggle, no tenant-config flag, no aggregate-emit endpoint, no anonymized payload schema, no scheduling layer. The `Foundations` track per spec §4.4 owns the broader telemetry plumbing decision; T5 owns the product-side strategy: what we capture, what we never capture, how it surfaces in the Admin Dashboard, and what the opt-in UI looks like.
- **Foundations-side prerequisites that don't exist today:** tenant-config storage location for the opt-in flag, transport service for HTTPS POST, batching scheduler, retry-with-backoff layer, privacy-notice surface in SP admin center, anonymized-aggregate compute pipeline (client-side before send vs server-side after receive). All of these are net-new infrastructure that Foundations must land before T5.D8's emitter shim can flush a single signal beyond the local no-op buffer; the lack of any one of them keeps D8 in degraded-shim mode (compiles, type-checks the never-captured field list, but emit() returns immediately).
- **Local-only stats that could be exposed without sending.** Today the Admin Dashboard already surfaces aggregate signals from `SearchHistory` (`SearchInsightsPanel.tsx:291-559` — daily volume, click-through rate, top queries, top zero-result queries, top users) with no external send. This is the model for T5: signals computed from tenant-local data, displayed to the admin, and (only with explicit opt-in) optionally exported as anonymized aggregates.

Closed/Changed-Form items already in the T5 surface (per Appendix A): INC-005 (base refiner query `pageSize` corrected — the kind of off-by-one diagnostic gap that the DebugPanel Query tab is well-positioned to surface). Still-Open items in T5's path: UX-005 Changed-Form (zero-results panel manual refresh — owning track T4.D7 since the polish lives in the admin dashboard, but T5 borders on the same observability story); UX-006 Still-Open (Health tab missing user/vertical breakdown — T4.D7); UX-007 Still-Open (Insights CTR not time-weighted — T4.D7).

#### Gap to "amazing"

The audience profile is "any SPFx-capable tenant, self-serve, no SI hand-holding" — and T5 is the differentiator that prevents the worst tenant outcome: a user files a ticket that says "search is broken" and the admin has nothing to give the support engineer except "we'll need to reproduce it on our end." PnP Modern Search v4 is a pure black box (Appendix C "Debug FAB / DebugPanel (Query/Network/State/Logs/Errors)" — Better, but only because PnP has nothing); SP Search ships ~50% of the moat and leaves the polished half exposed. The gaps cluster in five places, kept distinct between local diagnostics and telemetry per spec §4.3.

**On the local-diagnostics side:** **First, the spec-prescribed tabs are partially missing.** Spec §4.3 names five tabs (Query / Network / State / Logs / Errors); SP Search ships four (Query / State / Config / Log) where the Log tab merges Errors and the Network tab does not exist at all. A support engineer debugging "why is this user seeing a 12-second result panel" needs per-call timing across the search query, vertical-count query, base-refiner query, coverage query, and SearchManager list reads — none of those are captured today beyond the single-slot `lastQuery`. **Second, the FAB is mounted on one web part.** A page hosting Box + Filters + Verticals + Manager but no Results renders no debug surface at all on `?debug=1`. The DebugCollector silently collects events from those web parts but the user has no way to view them. **Third, error surfacing is fragmented.** Five web parts use Fluent `MessageBar`, one DataGrid uses an ad-hoc `<div>` toast, several spots fall through to `state.error` rendered inline, three different `ErrorBoundary` shapes (toolkit, custom, layout-fallback) — no shared pattern means each new failure mode invents its own UI. The spfx-toolkit `Toast` / `ToastProvider` listed in CLAUDE.md as adopted is in fact unused. **Fourth, "why no results" stops at four cookie-cutter copy variants.** The orchestrator knows enough at the moment of a zero-result return to surface "removing FileType:pdf would have returned 47 results", "your queryTemplate token `{Site.URL}` resolved to a scope with zero items", "the People vertical is routed to a missing dataProviderId — falling back to SharePoint Search", or "your refiner `Authoer` is not a valid managed property" — none of those diagnostic nudges exist today. **Fifth, the support-bundle export does not exist.** A real ticket flow needs an admin or end user to attach a single artifact (state snapshot + recent network calls + current config + recent errors + browser/locale/version metadata) that the engineer can paste into a repro. There is no "Export support bundle" button, no `.json` artifact, no copy-to-clipboard summary. The Admin Dashboard's screenshot-as-evidence path (per T4.D9 pre-flight tab) addresses tenant-readiness, not per-incident debugging.

**On the telemetry side:** the gap is total. There is no opt-in toggle in any property pane, no tenant-config flag, no allowlist of fields that may be emitted, no field-redaction discipline, no aggregation/sampling layer, no destination. The **Foundations** track per spec §4.4 owns the telemetry-plumbing infrastructure decision (where the bytes go, what the on/off switch looks like at the tenant level, how the privacy notice surfaces); T5 owns the **product-side strategy** that consumes that infrastructure: which aggregate signals are worth emitting (e.g. zero-result rate per vertical, query-latency P95, error class frequency), which fields are explicitly forbidden from ever being captured (query text, user identity, result titles, URLs, tenant names, list item content — per spec §4.3), and how the opt-in surfaces in the property pane next to a clear "what we collect / what we never collect" copy block. Without T5 carrying its half of the contract, Foundations ships plumbing with nothing meaningful to plumb; with T5's half but no Foundations infrastructure, the product gains a property pane toggle that does nothing. Both halves must align before either ships.

#### Deliverables

**Local diagnostics deliverables (D1–D7).**

1. **Mount DebugFab on every user-facing web part with portal-shared DebugPanel singleton**
   - **Description:** Today `DebugFab` + `DebugPanel` (`src/webparts/spSearchResults/components/DebugFab.tsx:1-35`, `DebugPanel.tsx:1-458`) are physically located inside the Results web part and rendered only by `SpSearchResults.tsx:71-75, 839-848`. Move both files to `src/libraries/spSearchStore/debug/` (next to `DebugCollector.ts`) so the library component owns them and every web part can import them via `@store/debug`. Each user-facing web part (Box, Filters, Verticals, Manager, Admin Manager) renders `<DebugFab>` conditionally on `DebugCollector.isActive()` from its root component. Use a window-backed singleton `__sp_search_debug_panel__` (mirror of `__sp_search_context_map__` per `storeRegistry.ts:36-54`) to ensure that — when N web parts on the same page each render a FAB — only ONE panel instance opens at a time (otherwise five FABs spawn five overlapping panels). A page that hosts Box + Filters + Verticals + Manager but no Results renders the FAB on the topmost web part by DOM order; clicking opens the singleton panel. The panel's `store` prop becomes `store?: StoreApi<ISearchStore>` (optional) and the State tab degrades gracefully when no store is passed (e.g. on a Manager-only page) by falling back to "State requires a Search Box, Results, Filters, or Verticals web part on this page." Held at P1 (not P0) because the failure mode is "no debug surface on a page-without-Results" — workaround is "add a Results web part to the page" — friction-multiplying but not install-blocking.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("Debug FAB feature completeness"). Today's "FAB only on Results" failure mode is invisible until an admin builds a Box-only or Manager-only page and discovers `?debug=1` does nothing — which is exactly the page shape T2 / T3 / T4 deliverables produce (e.g. T3.D5 multi-context guide showcases multi-context pages where Results may live in a separate section from the Box).
   - **Effort:** M
   - **Priority:** P1
   - **Depends on:** none
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("Debug FAB feature completeness"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `grep -rn 'DebugFab\|DebugPanel' src/webparts` returns hits only in `spSearchResults/components/`; the other 5 web parts feed events into DebugCollector but render no surface
   - **Acceptance signal:** On a page hosting Box + Filters + Verticals + Manager (no Results), opening with `?debug=1` renders the FAB on the Box web part; clicking opens the singleton DebugPanel; State tab shows the "No store on this page" graceful-degradation copy. On a page hosting all 6 web parts, only one FAB renders (topmost by DOM order); clicking from any other web part is a no-op (FAB hidden). Unit test in `tests/debug/debugFabSingleton.test.ts` asserts the window-singleton de-dup behavior across N mounts.

2. **Network tab + per-call timing across all DebugCollector consumers**
   - **Description:** Replace the single-slot `lastQuery: IQueryDebugInfo | undefined` (`DebugCollector.ts:11`) with a ring buffer `recentNetworkCalls: INetworkCall[]` (cap 50, mirror of `MAX_EVENTS = 200` at `:4`). Define `INetworkCall { id, timestamp, kind: 'search' | 'verticalCount' | 'baseRefiner' | 'coverage' | 'managerList' | 'graphPresence' | 'taxonomy', label, durationMs, requestSummary, responseSummary?, error? }` in `IDebugTypes.ts`. Wire emission from: (a) `SearchOrchestrator._executeProviderWithRetry` (any provider call — `:344-360`, `:582`); (b) `CoverageStatsService.fetchStats` (`:62-244`); (c) `SearchManagerService` PnPjs list calls (wrap the existing `console.log '[SP Search] loadX: loaded N items'` pattern at `:467, 565, 617, 1117` to also emit a network-call entry); (d) `GraphSearchProvider` Graph calls; (e) `TaxonomyService` term lookups. Each emission writes a `requestSummary` (kind, target, params count) and a `responseSummary` (status, item count, byte size if cheap). Add a fifth tab "Network" to DebugPanel (`:382-387`) rendering rows with timing badges (re-use the green/yellow/red `timingClass()` at `:17-21`) and a per-row click-to-expand JSON tree for request / response. **PII discipline (T5 contract):** the Network tab MUST redact query text from `requestSummary.params` by replacing it with `'[redacted: queryText]'` when `kind === 'search'` — view-source on the panel must not expose user-typed search terms even though the panel is local-only (defense-in-depth for screen-share scenarios).
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit Network tab scope item — today none of the 30+ network calls surface a per-call timing or payload trace, so the support engineer debugging "this page took 12 seconds to render" has nothing to triage from. The single-slot `lastQuery` shows the most recent search but not the four parallel calls (vertical count, base refiner, coverage, manager) that landed before or after.
   - **Effort:** L (high end — 30+ SearchManagerService call sites + 8 emission patterns + new ring buffer interface + new tab)
   - **Priority:** P0
   - **Depends on:** none
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("Debug FAB feature completeness (Query / Network / State / Logs / Errors tabs)"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `IDebugTypes.ts:11, 25-27` shows single-slot `lastQuery`; `grep -n DebugCollector src/libraries/spSearchStore/services` returns 0 hits — service-layer calls are invisible to the DebugCollector
   - **Acceptance signal:** Open DebugPanel with `?debug=1` after a single search — Network tab lists 4–6 rows (main search, vertical count, base refiner if applicable, coverage if Manager loaded, plus any TaxonomyService calls); each row shows kind, target, duration with green/yellow/red badge, click-to-expand JSON. PII assertion: search-kind row's `params.queryText` reads `[redacted: queryText]` rather than the raw user input. Unit test in `tests/debug/networkTab.test.ts` asserts the redaction policy and the buffer cap (50).

3. **Errors tab with stack-trace formatting + group-by-class aggregation**
   - **Description:** Split the Errors view out of the merged Log tab (`DebugPanel.tsx:316-371`) into a fifth tab "Errors" (alongside the new "Network" tab from D2). The Errors tab consumes the same `ERROR`-typed events from `DebugCollector.getEvents()` but renders: (a) a top-level group-by-`error.message`-class summary ("3 occurrences of 'Search failed: 401'"); (b) per-occurrence rows with formatted stack trace using a small helper (split `error.stack` lines, mark frames originating in SP Search source vs `node_modules` with a leading badge); (c) a "Copy as bug report" per-row button that produces a markdown-formatted snippet with timestamp + message + truncated stack + the corresponding `lastQuery` snapshot (PII-redacted per D2's policy). Source-mapped frames are best-effort (depend on whether SPFx ships sourcemaps in production — typically no; document this in the panel header so the support engineer knows what to expect). Keep the Log tab focused on `SEARCH | FILTER | VERTICAL | URL | INIT` with the ERROR checkbox removed (or kept disabled with a tooltip "Errors are now in their own tab"). T5.D7's support bundle (below) consumes the Errors tab's grouped output verbatim.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit Errors tab scope item. Today an admin who sees the FAB pulse red (`DebugFab.tsx:14-21`) clicks through to a Log tab where the error is one row among 200; finding the stack trace requires `JSON.stringify(event.data)` round-trip parsing in DevTools. This is the single longest path between "something broke" and "I can describe it" in the current product.
   - **Effort:** M
   - **Priority:** P0
   - **Depends on:** Deliverable 2 (Network tab refactor lands tab-registration plumbing; Errors tab consumes same plumbing)
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("Debug FAB feature completeness (Query / Network / State / Logs / Errors tabs)"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `grep -n 'ERROR' src/webparts/spSearchResults/components/DebugPanel.tsx` shows ERROR is one filter checkbox among six (`:316, 344-355`) with no dedicated render path
   - **Acceptance signal:** Trigger 3 search failures with the same backend error — Errors tab shows "3 occurrences" group with one row expanded by default; stack trace renders with SP Search frames highlighted and `node_modules` frames dimmed; "Copy as bug report" copies a markdown block with PII-redacted query text and full stack. Manual: every `spLog.error` (post-D6) or `console.error` (pre-D6) from `SearchOrchestrator` produces a corresponding Errors tab entry within 100ms.

4. **DebugPanel tab-registration API for cross-track tab contributions (T3.D8 contract)**
   - **Description:** Replace the hard-coded `TABS` array at `DebugPanel.tsx:382-387` with a `registerDebugTab(id: string, label: string, render: (ctx: IDebugTabContext) => React.ReactElement, options?: { defaultExpanded?: boolean; sortOrder?: number })` API on the new `src/libraries/spSearchStore/debug/debugTabRegistry.ts` module. Built-in tabs (Query / Network / State / Config / Log / Errors from D2 + D3) self-register via the same API at module load time. Third-party / cross-track contributions (per T3.D8 multi-context tab) call `registerDebugTab('multi-context', 'Multi-Context', renderMultiContextTab)` from their own module. The panel renders tabs in `sortOrder` then registration order. `IDebugTabContext` exposes `{ store?: StoreApi<ISearchStore>; debugCollector: typeof DebugCollector }` so contributed tabs read from the same data sources without circular dependency on the panel. Export the registry from `@store/debug/index.ts` next to `DebugCollector`. **Cross-track contract for T3.D8:** T5.D4 ships this registry by the time T3.D8 (`hasStore` / `getStore` audit panel for runtime context inspection) needs to land its Multi-Context tab — T3.D8's `Depends on` list already names "T5 DebugPanel composition (concrete contract: tab-registration API; fallback: direct edit to DebugPanel.tsx)" so the contract is reciprocal. P1 (not P0) because the fallback (direct edit to `DebugPanel.tsx`) is documented and unblocks T3.D8 in the absence of D4 — the registry is the durable shape, not the only path.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator and (a) T3 differentiator (cross-track). T3.D8's Multi-Context tab is a real product surface that needs to compose into the same DebugPanel; without this registry T3.D8 ships in fallback mode (direct edit to a file owned by T5), which is the failure mode that produced today's "DebugFab only on Results" gap (D1) — coupling between web parts and the debug surface should flow through library-component APIs, not through cross-folder imports.
   - **Effort:** M
   - **Priority:** P1
   - **Depends on:** Deliverable 1 (DebugPanel relocation to library component is the file move that makes this registry reachable from non-Results call sites)
   - **Source:** Phase 6.5 discovery: `DebugPanel.tsx:382-387` hard-codes the `TABS` array; T3.D8 (`### T3. Multi-Instance / Multi-Context` in this doc) explicitly names this contract in its `Depends on` line
   - **Acceptance signal:** `import { registerDebugTab } from '@store/debug'` resolves; calling `registerDebugTab('test-tab', 'Test', () => <div>hello</div>, { sortOrder: 99 })` from a unit test mounts the tab as the rightmost entry in the panel. T3.D8's `MultiContextTab` registers with `id='multi-context'` and the panel renders it without any code change to `DebugPanel.tsx`. Unit test in `tests/debug/debugTabRegistry.test.ts` covers (a) built-in tabs auto-register, (b) custom tab landed in correct sortOrder slot, (c) duplicate id warns and keeps first registration.

5. **"Why no results" diagnostic panel — orchestrator knows more than it tells the EmptyState**
   - **Description:** Extend `EmptyState` (`SpSearchResults.tsx:402-444`) to render a collapsible "Diagnostics" section below the existing four context-aware copy variants. Fed by a new `IZeroResultsDiagnostic` payload computed in the orchestrator at the moment a search returns zero items: (a) **filter-counterfactual** — for each active filter, run a parallel lightweight refiners-only query without that filter (re-using the existing `_executeProviderWithRetry` pattern at `SearchOrchestrator.ts:344-360` with `pageSize: 0`) and report "Removing 'FileType: pdf' would return ~47 results"; cache for the current `(queryText, activeFilters)` tuple to avoid re-running on every render. (b) **token-resolution trace** — surface the resolved `queryText` after `{searchTerms}` / `{Site.URL}` / `{Page.Property}` substitution from `TokenService` so admins can see "your token `{Page.Department}` resolved to empty string". (c) **provider routing trace** — surface "vertical 'people' is routed to provider 'graph-search' (resolved from `dataProviderId`)" so a misrouted vertical is visible. (d) **refiner sanity** — when a managed property in `state.filterConfig` returns zero buckets in the refiner response, surface "refiner `Authoer` returned no buckets — verify managed property name". Diagnostics surface ONLY when `items.length === 0 && hasSearched && !isLoading`, hidden by default behind a "Why no results?" disclosure button so the empty state stays clean for end users. Edit-mode + admin-mode see the diagnostics expanded by default; end-user mode keeps them collapsed. Token / provider / refiner traces ALWAYS render if the disclosure is opened (they cost no extra calls); filter-counterfactual is gated on `enableZeroResultDiagnostics: boolean` (default `false`) on Results web part property pane to keep parallel calls opt-in for tenants worried about extra search-call cost. **New orchestrator state fields:** the always-render diagnostics require the orchestrator to retain three new fields per search cycle: `lastResolvedQueryText: string` (post-token-substitution), `lastRefinerBuckets: IRefinerBucket[]` (response.refiners shape after the search returns), `lastResolvedProviderId: string` (per-vertical routing decision). All three are local-only (no telemetry emission) and overwrite per cycle (no history retention). Add to `IOrchestratorState` interface in `SearchOrchestrator.ts`.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit "why no results" panel scope item. Today the orchestrator computes `state.querySuggestion` from the search response (`SearchOrchestrator.ts:403`) and surfaces it as "Did you mean…" — that's the entire diagnostic pipeline for zero-result recoveries. The orchestrator knows about token resolution, provider routing, and refiner sanity at the moment of zero return; not surfacing those three signals throws away free product value.
   - **Effort:** L
   - **Priority:** P0
   - **Depends on:** Deliverable 2 (filter-counterfactual queries are network calls — D2's Network tab is the surface that proves they're cached and not stomping the user's actual search budget)
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("'why no results' panel"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `SpSearchResults.tsx:402-444` `EmptyState` has 4 copy variants and 2 generic recovery affordances with no diagnostic body
   - **Acceptance signal:** Search for an obscure term with two filters active producing zero results — empty state renders the existing copy plus a "Why no results?" disclosure; opening it shows three diagnostic rows: filter-counterfactual (when `enableZeroResultDiagnostics === true`), token-resolution trace, refiner sanity check. Mistype a refiner managed property and search — refiner-sanity row reads "refiner 'Authoer' returned no buckets — verify managed property name in property pane". Unit test in `tests/orchestrator/zeroResultDiagnostic.test.ts` covers all four diagnostic shapes with mock provider responses.

6. **Logging discipline sweep — central log shim with PII redaction + production gate**
   - **Description:** Introduce `src/libraries/spSearchStore/logging/spLog.ts` exposing `spLog.debug | info | warn | error` with three contracts: (a) **Severity filter** — debug + info silenced unless `?debug=1` is set OR `localStorage.getItem('sp-search:log-level') === 'debug'`; warn + error always log. (b) **Field redaction** — calls accept a structured payload object `{ message, fields?: Record<string, unknown> }`; fields named `queryText`, `kqlText`, `loginName`, `email`, `userPrincipalName`, `displayName`, `searchUrl` are auto-replaced with `'[redacted]'` before write. Free-form string `message` is allowed to contain user content but is the caller's responsibility — the shim warns once via static-analysis-friendly comment ("If your message contains user input, prefer `fields` over interpolation"). (c) **Namespace** — all logs prefix `[SP Search:<area>]` where `<area>` is set per file (`spLog.namespace('orchestrator')`). Sweep the four `console.log/warn/error` sites in `SearchOrchestrator.ts:282-285, 290-296, 459-464, 490-495` to use `spLog.debug({ message: 'First search starting', fields: { providerId, queryText: state.queryText } })` — the redaction policy zeroes out `queryText` before write so the console no longer leaks user input. Sweep the 31+ `console.*` sites in `src/libraries/` and 9 in `src/webparts/` (`grep -rn 'console\.' src/libraries src/webparts | wc -l` returns 40 today). Production builds gate `spLog.debug` and `spLog.info` to no-op via webpack `DefinePlugin` (`process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`); warn + error always emit. Pairs with Foundations security sweep (BUG-004 fix is the security half; logging discipline is the privacy half). (Heft-side build gate via `fast-serve/webpack.extend.js` pattern, since `gulpfile.js` no longer exists post-1.22 migration — see Foundations track for the broader Heft webpack-extension story).
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator and (b) security (PII protection in browser console). Spec §4.3 T5 explicit "logging discipline (avoid PII)" scope item. Today the orchestrator writes the user's query text to the browser console four times per search at info/error severity — anyone with screen-share access sees searches like "performance review John Smith Q3" in the console. This is the single most visible PII exposure in the product and the fix costs one shim file plus a sweep PR.
   - **Effort:** L
   - **Priority:** P0
   - **Depends on:** none
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("logging discipline (avoid PII)"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `grep -n 'state\.queryText' src/libraries/spSearchStore/orchestrator/SearchOrchestrator.ts` returns 4 console-write sites at `:293, 463, 493, 501`
   - **Acceptance signal:** Open DevTools console with `?debug=1` removed — searching for "performance review" produces zero console output containing the literal string "performance review". With `?debug=1` set, console output reads `[SP Search:orchestrator] First search starting providerId=sharepoint-search queryText=[redacted]`. Unit test in `tests/logging/spLog.test.ts` covers (a) PII field redaction, (b) production-mode silence of debug/info, (c) namespace prefix on every output, (d) warn/error always emit.

7. **Exportable support bundle — single-click ".json" artifact for incident triage**
   - **Description:** Add an "Export support bundle" button to the DebugPanel header (`DebugPanel.tsx:432-437` adjacent to the existing close button) that produces a single `sp-search-support-bundle-<isoTimestamp>.json` download containing: (a) **state snapshot** — current store state for every context in `__sp_search_context_map__` (queryText replaced with `'[redacted]'`; activeFilters keys preserved but values redacted; filterConfig + verticals + selectedProperties preserved unredacted as they're admin config); (b) **recent network calls** — D2's `recentNetworkCalls` ring buffer (50 most recent) with per-call timing + status, request bodies redacted per D2's PII policy; (c) **recent events** — DebugCollector's 200-event ring buffer with the same redaction; (d) **recent errors** — D3's grouped Errors output with stack traces; (e) **config snapshot** — `webPartConfigs` Map serialized (manifest properties only, no user data); (f) **environment metadata** — SP Search package version (read from `package-solution.json` via `webPart.dataVersion` per existing pattern), browser user-agent, locale, viewport, theme name, the four T3 multi-context fields (`window.__sp_search_context_map__` size + per-context urlPrefix + initialized flag); (g) **redaction manifest** — explicit JSON section listing every field that was redacted and why ("`queryText` redacted per T5 PII policy — set `?debug=1&support-bundle-include-pii=1` to override; never share unredacted bundle outside your tenant"). Provide a "Copy to clipboard" alternative to the file download for tenants where downloads are blocked. Document the override-flag policy in `docs/admin-guide.md` Support section (new) so a security-aware admin can intentionally include PII for an internal-only ticket. **Bundle size cap:** total bundle never exceeds 500 KB. Internal section caps: `webPartConfigs` truncates at 50 KB, `network` ring buffer at 50 KB, `events` ring buffer at 50 KB, `errors` at 50 KB. When a section truncates, the bundle includes a `truncations: [{section, reason, totalSize}]` manifest so the support engineer knows why.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit "exportable support bundle (state snapshot + recent network calls + config)" scope item, AND Journey A Step 12 [Polish] (the only T5-tagged Journey A item explicitly names this gap: "no 'send a support bundle' / 'export current state' path that an admin can give a user to attach to a ticket"). Closing this gap converts SP Search from "we'll need to reproduce on our end" to "paste the bundle into the ticket" — the single most leverageable shift in incident triage cost. Held at P1 (not P0) because the gap is a [Polish] severity item with the documented workaround "open DevTools, copy the Network tab + console manually" — friction-multiplying but not install-blocking. **Sprint sequencing note:** P1 placement assumes the workaround "open DevTools and copy console output" remains viable. After D6 (PII redaction) lands, that workaround produces `[redacted]` for queryText/userId/etc., making D7 the only path to pre-redaction support context. Recommend D7 ships in the same Sprint as D6, not after — coordinate sequencing in the per-track plan.
   - **Effort:** L
   - **Priority:** P1
   - **Depends on:** Deliverable 1 (multi-web-part FAB), Deliverable 2 (Network tab buffer), Deliverable 3 (Errors tab grouped output), Deliverable 6 (PII-redaction policy is shared with the bundle exporter)
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("exportable support bundle"); Journey A Step 12 [Polish]
   - **Acceptance signal:** Click "Export support bundle" — downloads `sp-search-support-bundle-2026-05-02T14-30-22.json` (~50–200 KB depending on event-buffer fill); opening the file shows seven top-level sections (state, network, events, errors, config, env, redactions); searching the file for the literal user query string returns 0 matches; the redactions section lists every redacted field with rationale. "Copy to clipboard" alternative writes the same JSON to the clipboard. Manual on a real ticket: paste the bundle into a GitHub issue body — engineer can reproduce the failure mode end-to-end without further questions for queries / filters / errors. Downloaded `.json` bundle is ≤ 500 KB on a fully-loaded multi-context page with 6 web parts × 30 properties; truncation manifest present when limits hit. Unit test in `tests/debug/supportBundle.test.ts` covers (a) all seven sections present, (b) query-text redaction holds, (c) override flag includes PII when set.

**Telemetry deliverables (D8–D9).**

8. **Telemetry strategy + opt-in property pane surface (paired with Foundations infrastructure)**
   - **Description:** T5 owns the **product-side telemetry strategy** that consumes Foundations' opt-in / tenant-config / privacy-notice plumbing. Three artifacts: (a) **`docs/telemetry.md`** — authoritative spec for what may be captured (proposed initial set: zero-result rate per vertical, search-call P50/P95 latency, error class frequency, layout-switch counts, vertical-switch counts) and what is **never** captured (verbatim list per spec §4.3: query text, user identity, result titles, URLs, tenant names, list item content). (b) **`ITelemetrySignal` interface + `TelemetryEmitter` shim in `src/libraries/spSearchStore/telemetry/`** — emitter is a no-op until Foundations' opt-in flag is set; when enabled, accepts `emit(signal: ITelemetrySignal)` calls and aggregates locally before handing to Foundations' transport layer (no direct fetch from T5 code — Foundations owns the wire). The shim enforces the never-captured field list at compile time via TypeScript discriminated union — `ITelemetrySignal` cannot type-check if it includes a `queryText` or `userId` field. (c) **Property pane surface** — add a `Telemetry` group on the Admin Manager property pane (T4.D6's Path B Admin Manager fork is the natural home) with one toggle "Send aggregate usage signals to your tenant administrator" (default `false`), an inline `MessageBar` linking to `docs/telemetry.md`, and a link "View what we send" that opens a Panel with a live preview of the next aggregate batch (so admins enabling it see exactly what leaves the browser before committing). Wire `SearchOrchestrator` (`:442-448` SEARCH event), `verticalSlice.ts:11` (vertical switch), and `filterSlice.ts:137` (filter set) to call `TelemetryEmitter.emit({ kind: ..., aggregateField: ... })` — emissions are no-ops unless the toggle is on AND Foundations infrastructure is wired. **Proposed destination shape (T5-side strategy, Foundations-side plumbing):** admin-configured HTTPS POST endpoint with JSON body `{batch: ITelemetrySignal[]}`. Foundations owns: actual transport (auth, retry-with-backoff, batching cadence, exponential-backoff on failure), tenant-config storage location for the opt-in flag, privacy-notice surface in SP admin center. T5 ships: `TelemetryEmitter.emit(signal)` shim that buffers when destination is unconfigured (no-op) and POSTs when destination + opt-in are both set. The single-endpoint-per-tenant model keeps the configuration matrix small enough for self-serve; multi-endpoint/per-feature destinations are explicitly out of scope.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit "telemetry hook strategy (opt-in, anonymous, what fields)" scope item. Without T5's strategy, Foundations ships infrastructure with nothing to plumb; without Foundations' infrastructure, T5's strategy ships a property-pane toggle that does nothing. The T5 contract is to define the schema, the redaction discipline, and the property-pane surface so that when Foundations lands the wire (per Foundations track), the product immediately gains a meaningful telemetry surface that a security-conscious admin can review before opting in.
   - **Effort:** L
   - **Priority:** P1
   - **Depends on:** Foundations.D9 (Foundations owns transport `TelemetryTransport.ts`, opt-in storage `SearchTelemetryConfig` list, privacy-notice `docs/privacy-notice.md`, and per-user consent `SearchTelemetryOptIn` list per spec §4.4; T5.D8 supplies the per-emitter `ITelemetrySignal` schema + emitter shim + property pane toggle that consume them); Deliverable 6 (PII redaction shim is the shared language for what "never captured" means in code); Deliverable 7 (support bundle's `redactions` manifest is the documentation pattern that telemetry's "what we send" Panel mirrors); T4.D6 (Admin Manager fork is the natural home for the property pane toggle — coordinate placement with the Admin Manager admin-only property page)
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("telemetry hook strategy (opt-in, anonymous, what fields)"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `grep -rn 'telemetry\|appInsights\|sendBeacon' src` returns 0 hits across the source tree
   - **Acceptance signal:** `docs/telemetry.md` exists with the captured / never-captured lists explicit. `ITelemetrySignal` type cannot compile when given `{ kind: 'search', queryText: string }` — TypeScript discriminated union rejects forbidden fields. Property pane Telemetry group on Admin Manager renders a default-off toggle; opening "View what we send" Panel shows a sample batch with no PII. Toggling on with Foundations infrastructure not wired produces a graceful "Telemetry transport not configured by tenant administrator" inline message; toggling on with infrastructure wired begins emitting aggregate signals (verified via Network tab from D2 — outbound emissions appear as a new `kind: 'telemetryFlush'` row).

9. **Telemetry-derived insights surfaced in Admin Dashboard (consume what we emit)**
   - **Description:** When telemetry is opted in (per D8) AND Foundations infrastructure aggregates signals across users, the Admin Dashboard's existing four panels (Coverage / Quality / Health / Insights, owned by T4.D7) gain an opt-in "Aggregate" view toggle that switches the underlying data source from the per-user `SearchHistory` list to the tenant-aggregated telemetry feed. Concretely: (a) `SearchInsightsPanel.tsx:291-559` adds a "Source: per-user history | aggregate telemetry" ChoiceGroup at the top; aggregate mode reads from a new `getAggregateInsights(daysBack)` method on Foundations' transport-side service. (b) `ZeroResultsPanel.tsx:32-64` `aggregateEntries` gains an aggregate-mode branch that bypasses the per-user grouping and reads pre-aggregated zero-result counts. (c) `QualityMetricsSection.tsx` gains an "Across all users" badge when aggregate mode is active. (d) Admin sees a new "Telemetry coverage" card in the Coverage tab indicating "X% of tenant users have opted in" so the admin knows whether the aggregate view is statistically meaningful. T5's role is to **define the schema** the dashboard consumes — the actual transport, opt-in counting, and per-user enforcement live in Foundations. **Opt-in percentage source:** computed locally from a SharePoint list (`SearchTelemetryOptIn`) write of opt-in events at consent time. Each row stores `{ConsentTimestamp, ConsentVersion, AnonHash}` where `AnonHash = SHA-256(tenantId + userPrincipalName + 'sp-search-telemetry-v1') -> first 8 chars`. The hash is irreversible (no rainbow table for SHA-256 with a per-tenant salt prefix), so the list shows opt-in *count* per tenant without identifying *who* opted in. The aggregate percentage is computed as `optInCount / totalActiveUsersInLastNDays` where the denominator comes from SharePoint's existing usage analytics. If the privacy-review process objects even to this anonymized count, the card degrades to a binary 'Telemetry: enabled / disabled' state with no percentage.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (a) T5 differentiator. Spec §4.3 T5 explicit "Admin Dashboard analytics (Health + Insights)" scope item. Today the dashboard answers "what did the users I can see search for?" using the per-user `SearchHistory` list (constrained by Author filter per Data Rule #1). With opt-in telemetry the dashboard can answer "what does the tenant look like in aggregate?" without expanding the cross-user-read surface owned by `loadAllHistoryForInsights`. This is the durable answer to UX-006 ("Health tab missing user/vertical breakdown") at scales where per-user enumeration is rate-limited or privacy-restricted.
   - **Effort:** M
   - **Priority:** P2
   - **Depends on:** Deliverable 8 (telemetry strategy + emitter shim); Foundations.D9 (transport `TelemetryTransport.ts` + per-user opt-in `SearchTelemetryOptIn` list — the "Telemetry coverage: X% of users opted in" card reads the per-user opt-in count from this list); T4.D7 (Admin Dashboard depth bundle is the surface this deliverable adds the toggle to — coordinate render slots so D9's ChoiceGroup doesn't fight T4.D7's pivot toggles)
   - **Source:** spec §4.3 T5 explicit scope item ("Admin Dashboard analytics (Health + Insights)"); Phase 6.5 discovery: `SearchInsightsPanel.tsx:291-559` reads exclusively from per-user history with no aggregate path; Appendix A UX-006 (Still-Open) pins the per-user-only limitation
   - **Acceptance signal:** Telemetry opt-in toggle ON + Foundations transport wired — Insights tab ChoiceGroup switches to "Aggregate telemetry" and the rendered numbers come from the tenant-aggregated feed; Coverage tab shows the new "Telemetry coverage: 47% of users opted in" card. Toggle OFF or Foundations transport not configured — ChoiceGroup is hidden and the dashboard reads exclusively from per-user `SearchHistory` (today's behavior).

##### Coverage walk (spec §4.3 T5 scope item → mapping)

- **Debug FAB feature completeness (Query / Network / State / Logs / Errors tabs)** → Current State proves 4 of 5 tabs ship today via `DebugPanel.tsx:382-387` (Query / State / Config / Log; Errors merged into Log; Network missing entirely); D2 (Network tab + per-call timing), D3 (Errors tab split + grouping), D1 (FAB on every web part), D4 (tab-registration API)
- **Error surfacing patterns (toasts vs panels vs inline)** → Current State proves three styles ship today (`MessageBar` 5+ web parts, ad-hoc DataGrid `<div>` toast, inline render, ErrorBoundary in 5 web parts) with no shared abstraction; D3 (Errors tab is the central viewer) plus T5 Out of Scope item 3 (cross-web-part Toast adoption) — toolkit `Toast` adoption is owned by Foundations as a CLAUDE.md-vs-code consistency fix, not a T5 deliverable
- **"Why no results" panel** → D5 (filter-counterfactual + token-resolution trace + provider routing trace + refiner sanity); Current State proves only `querySuggestion` "Did you mean…" surfaces today
- **Telemetry hook strategy (opt-in, anonymous, what fields)** → D8 (strategy + emitter shim + property pane surface); Current State proves zero telemetry implementation
- **Admin Dashboard analytics (Health + Insights)** → D9 (telemetry-aggregate view toggle); T4.D7 owns the per-panel depth (UX-005/006/007 closure) — T5.D9 adds the orthogonal aggregate-source dimension on top of T4.D7's structural improvements
- **Exportable support bundle (state snapshot + recent network calls + config)** → D7 (single-click `.json` export); Current State proves zero export path today
- **Logging discipline (avoid PII)** → D6 (central log shim + redaction + production gate); Current State proves 4 raw `console.log(..., state.queryText, ...)` sites at `SearchOrchestrator.ts:293, 463, 493, 501`
- **Required local-vs-telemetry split (spec §4.3)** → Section structure splits Current State into (A) Local diagnostics + (B) Telemetry; Deliverables split D1–D7 (local) + D8–D9 (telemetry); Coverage walk maintains the split per scope item

##### Effort total

**9 deliverables (4 P0 / 4 P1 / 1 P2)**: P0 = D2 (L) + D3 (M) + D5 (L) + D6 (L); P1 = D1 (M) + D4 (M) + D7 (L) + D8 (L); P2 = D9 (M). Effort tier midpoints (S ≤ 4h ≈ 0.5d; M = ½–1d, midpoint 0.75d; L = 1–3d, midpoint 2d). **Effort total: ~13.5 dev-days midpoint** (after I1 bumps D6 from M to L: 5×L + 4×M = 10 + 3 = 13d midpoint; range 10-20d). The ±5d range is driven by: (a) D6 may slip to L+ if any of the 40 `console.*` sites need contextual rewrites rather than mechanical replacement; (b) D7 + D8 carry coordination cost with Foundations transport plumbing — if Foundations defers telemetry transport entirely, D8 ships in degraded form and the upper-bound estimate doesn't apply. P0 admission rule (each P0 ties to a/b/c/d/e per spec §6): D2 ties (a) T5 differentiator — spec §4.3 T5 explicit Network tab scope item; D3 ties (a) T5 differentiator — spec §4.3 T5 explicit Errors tab scope item; D5 ties (a) T5 differentiator — spec §4.3 T5 explicit "why no results" panel scope item; D6 ties (b) security — concrete in-product PII exposure logged in Current State (`SearchOrchestrator.ts:293, 463, 493, 501` write `state.queryText` to console). D1 (multi-web-part FAB), D4 (tab-registration API), D7 (support bundle) held P1 because each has a documented workaround in the absence of the deliverable; D8 (telemetry strategy) gated on Foundations transport; D9 (telemetry-aggregate dashboard) gated on D8.

#### Out of scope for v1.0

- **External-send telemetry transport (the actual wire to Application Insights / Azure Monitor / custom endpoint).** Rationale: Foundations track per spec §4.4 explicitly owns telemetry plumbing — destination, on-off switch storage, tenant-level enforcement, privacy notice surface. T5.D8 supplies the schema + emitter shim + property pane that consumes the Foundations transport; without Foundations' wire, D8's emit() calls are no-ops by design. Splitting strategy from transport keeps T5 shippable independently of Foundations and prevents a single PR from straddling product strategy and infrastructure decisions.
- **Source-mapped stack traces in the Errors tab (D3).** Rationale: SPFx production builds typically ship without sourcemaps to keep `.sppkg` size down; chasing sourcemap delivery would require build-pipeline changes (Foundations) and is more complex than the line-number-formatted stacks D3 ships. Document the limitation in the Errors tab header so a support engineer reading a "Copy as bug report" snippet knows to expect minified frame names. Re-evaluate at v1.1 if Foundations' build-pipeline work makes sourcemap delivery cheap.
- **Real-time DebugPanel updates over BroadcastChannel for multi-tab inspection.** Rationale: A user with two tabs open today sees two independent DebugCollector singletons (window-keyed per tab); cross-tab event sync would need BroadcastChannel + per-tab event de-dup which adds substantial state-machine complexity for a use case (admin debugs across two tabs) that is not in the audience profile. Defer to v1.1+ if the per-tab limitation surfaces in real support tickets.
- **Recording / replay of search sessions (timeline scrubber that replays N seconds of state changes).** Rationale: would require capturing the full state delta stream into IndexedDB and a replay UI; rich but expensive. Today's State tab change-highlight (`DebugPanel.tsx:246-261`) and Log tab event ring buffer cover the same intent at 5% the implementation cost. Reject for v1.0; revisit v2.0 if the support pattern proves it.
- **Heatmap / click-tracking visualization in the Admin Dashboard.** Rationale: Click-through-rate per query already lands in `SearchInsightsPanel.tsx` via `clickedItems` aggregation; per-cell heatmaps add visualization complexity (canvas rendering, color scales, accessibility ARIA labels per cell) without adding actionable signal beyond the existing CTR-per-query column. T4.D7 owns the existing CTR work; T5 carries no separate heatmap deliverable.
- **Toast / ToastProvider adoption from spfx-toolkit.** Rationale: CLAUDE.md lists `Toast / ToastProvider` as adopted but `grep -rn 'spfx-toolkit/lib/components/Toast' src` returns 0 hits — this is a CLAUDE.md-vs-code documentation drift item that belongs to Foundations' docs sweep, not a T5 product deliverable. Error surfacing consistency (D3's central Errors tab) addresses the diagnostic half; the user-facing notification half (toast adoption for save/share/export confirmations) is owned by T1 / T2 / Foundations (whichever sweeps the documentation drift first).
- **Telemetry-driven A/B testing for layout / preset / filter defaults.** Rationale: A/B testing requires bucketing logic, persistent assignment storage, and statistical-significance calculation — none of which the audience profile demands at v1.0 ("self-serve any tenant"). T5 telemetry surfaces aggregate signals admins can read; experiment infrastructure is a different product shape. Defer indefinitely.
- **Cross-incident correlation IDs (request-id propagation through the search call graph).** Rationale: SharePoint Search backend has no correlation-id contract; the Graph backend supports `client-request-id` headers but single-provider correlation-id support without the SP-side equivalent would be inconsistent and could mislead engineers into believing they have full-call-graph correlation. Defer until both providers support it. The closest available signal is the per-request timestamp captured in D2's Network tab — sufficient for client-side incident triage.



---

## Part 3 — Foundations Track

#### Current state

Foundations is the cross-cutting plumbing every other track depends on but no single track owns: security hardening, the in-flight SPFx 1.22 / Heft migration, accessibility baseline, CI / release engineering, documentation, telemetry transport, and per-web-part performance budgets. Today the substrate is uneven: security got most of the load (BUG-004 closed plus a sanitizer in place), the SPFx 1.22 migration landed on a feature branch that has not merged, accessibility closed four of six March 22 items but ships no published WCAG conformance statement and no axe-core gate, CI/release engineering does not exist (no `.github/workflows/`, no CHANGELOG, no semver tags, package version pinned at `0.0.1`), documentation drifts in three places (no top-level README, CLAUDE.md still claims SPFx 1.21 + gulp, admin-guide describes Manager defaults that disagree with manifests), telemetry plumbing is zero, and the production bundle is 8–15 MB per web part with no documented budget or CI gate.

The actual Foundations surface, by file:

- **F-1 lint blocker — `npm run package` cannot produce `.sppkg`.** `src/styles/pnpPropertyControlsFix.ts:33` references the constant `PNP_COLLECTION_DATA_CSS` before its declaration on `:42`; ESLint rule `@typescript-eslint/no-use-before-define` raises it as `error`, which Heft's lint stage elevates to a build failure. SARIF output captured at `release/analysis-logs/lint.sarif` confirms: `"level": "error"`, `"text": "'PNP_COLLECTION_DATA_CSS' was used before it was defined."`. Both `npm run package` and `npm test` (Heft pipeline) halt at lint before TypeScript or Webpack runs. No `.sppkg` artifact is produced through documented commands. Fix is one mechanical reorder; the gate is the lint blocker.
- **F-2 broken `type-check` script.** `package.json:28` defines `"type-check": "heft build --clean --lite"`, but `--lite` is not a documented Heft CLI flag in current Heft 1.2.x releases. The script either fails or no-ops without exercising the type checker. The fallback `npx tsc --noEmit` against `tsconfig.json` passes (the type system itself is clean), so the breakage is in the script wrapper, not the underlying code. Misleading because docs (`docs/deployment-guide.md:18`) tell admins to run it before packaging.
- **SPFx 1.22 / Heft migration — unmerged feature branch.** `feat/spfx-1.22-heft-migration` is **91 commits ahead of `main`** (`git log --oneline main..HEAD | wc -l` = 91). Migration commits include: `c6dd4f1` (Heft config files + webpack patch), `a5f28c1` (Gulp → Heft build system), `77adef7` (SPFx 1.22.2 / spfx-toolkit type mismatch fix), `b4186e8` (Heft build errors — SASS, ESLint, source-map-loader), `bab3e9e` (PnP property controls CSS fix). Repo state at HEAD is functional under Heft (modulo F-1), but the branch has never been merged — admins who clone `main` get the prior SPFx 1.21 + gulp build chain, admins who clone the feature branch get the un-shipped Heft path. No merge criteria, no smoke checklist, no release tag.
- **Security sweep — narrow but recently audited.** `grep -rn "dangerouslySetInnerHTML" src` returns ONE site: `src/webparts/spSearchResults/components/ListLayout.tsx:69` rendering through the local `sanitizeSummaryHtml` at `src/webparts/spSearchResults/components/documentTitleUtils.ts:158`. `grep -rn "window\.location\.href" src` returns 7 sites (`src/libraries/spSearchStore/providers/QuickResultsSuggestionProvider.ts:80`, `src/webparts/spSearchBox/components/SpSearchBox.tsx:358` — BUG-004-hardened with `https?://` / `/` allowlist, `src/webparts/spSearchManager/components/SpSearchManager.tsx:369,548,644,646`, `src/webparts/spSearchResults/components/SpSearchResults.tsx:568,570`). `grep -rn "innerHTML" src` returns the same single React-rendered site as `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`. `grep -rn "eval(\|new Function(" src` returns zero hits. The `spfx-toolkit/lib/utilities/htmlUtils/sanitizeHtml` adopt-target from Appendix B (HTML sanitization) is **not yet integrated** (`grep -rn "sanitizeHtml\|spfx-toolkit/lib/utilities/htmlUtils" src` returns 0 hits) — the local sanitizer remains in place. Saved-search JSON `JSON.parse` + cast (SEC-004 Still-Open per Appendix A) at `SavedSearchList.tsx:76,163` is owned end-to-end by T2.D3.
- **Accessibility baseline.** `grep -rn "prefers-reduced-motion\|prefers-color-scheme" src` returns **0 hits** across the source tree — no motion-reduction respect anywhere. Per-component `aria-*` usage is uneven: 10 files report ARIA attribute usage with counts ranging 1–5 per file, concentrated in `src/webparts/spSearchBox/components/{KqlInput.tsx, KqlCompletionDropdown.tsx, QueryBuilder.tsx, SpSearchBox.tsx, SuggestionDropdown.tsx}` and `src/webparts/spSearchVerticals/components/{SpSearchVerticals.tsx, VerticalTab.tsx}` and three Manager components; the other 30+ component files have no `aria-*` attributes at all. `FocusTrapZone` / `FocusZone` not used (`grep -rn "FocusTrapZone\|FocusZone" src/webparts` returns 0 hits) — Filters drawer (T1.D1), detail panel (T1.D6), and ManageAccess panel (T2.D5) all need it. No skip-to-content link (`grep -rn "skip-to-(content|main)\|skipLink" src` returns 0 hits). No published WCAG conformance statement (`docs/accessibility.md` does not exist). Appendix A A11Y-004 (mode toggle div instead of fieldset) and A11Y-005 (scope selector aria-describedby missing) remain Still-Open. The audit closed 4 of 6 March 22 A11Y items but no axe-core / Lighthouse / Wave CI gate prevents regressions.
- **CI / release engineering.** **No `.github/` directory exists** in the repo (verified). No GitHub Actions workflow, no Azure Pipelines, no Jenkinsfile. `package.json:3` pins `version: "0.0.1"` — pinned at the SPFx generator default. `config/package-solution.json:6` ships `version: "1.0.13.0"` (incremented manually) but no semver convention is documented and no git tags exist (`git tag --list` returns empty per Appendix E). No `CHANGELOG.md`, no `CONTRIBUTING.md`, no `RELEASE.md` at the repo root. No automation to publish a `.sppkg` to GitHub Releases, an Azure Storage account, or a tenant app catalog. `solution.developer.mpnId = "Undefined-1.21.1"` (`config/package-solution.json:15`, also flagged in T4.D10) carries the SPFx generator default into shipped packages — visible to admins reviewing the package in the SharePoint admin "Apps you can add" pane. No PR template, no issue templates, no Dependabot or Renovate config. The whole release engineering surface is empty.
- **Documentation.** **No top-level `README.md` exists at the repo root** (`test -f /Users/hemantmane/Development/sp-search/README.md` reports "No README at repo root"). The `docs/` directory contains 5 admin-facing guides (`admin-guide.md` 285 lines, `deployment-guide.md` 171 lines, `extensibility-guide.md` 565 lines, `provisioning-guide.md` 147 lines, `pnp-modern-search-alignment.md` 121 lines) plus the in-progress launch audit + the 1,868-line requirements doc. No end-user docs (Journey A Step 12 [Confusion]; T2.D12 owns the end-user guide). No troubleshooting / FAQ. No contributing guide. `CLAUDE.md` is internally inconsistent with shipped code in three places: line 7 / line 48 still claim "SPFx 1.21.1" while `package.json:39-46` ships `@microsoft/sp-* ^1.22.2`; line 115 + lines 492–493 still prescribe `gulp serve` / `gulp bundle --ship` after the 1.22 migration replaced gulpfile.js with Heft (`a5f28c1`); line 58 + line 464 still list `Toast / ToastProvider` as adopted across all web parts despite `grep -rn 'spfx-toolkit/lib/components/Toast' src` returning 0 hits. `docs/admin-guide.md:221-226` claims four Manager toggles default to `true`; `SpSearchManagerWebPart.manifest.json:30-33` ships them all `false` (Journey A Step 10 [Confusion]). `docs/provisioning-guide.md:131-132` claims "no automatic background cleanup" while `SearchManagerService.ts:735-739` runs a 24h cleanup sweep (Journey A Step 10 [Confusion]). `docs/deployment-guide.md:21-22, 164` and `scripts/Setup-SPSearchSite.ps1:7,135` still prescribe gulp commands that no longer exist (Journey A Step 1 [Blocker], Step 1 [Confusion]).
- **Telemetry plumbing.** Zero. `grep -rn "telemetry\|analytics\|appInsights\|sendBeacon" src` returns 0 hits across the source tree (only `SearchInsightsPanel.tsx:291` matches the comment phrase "admin analytics surface" — not telemetry). No tenant-config storage location for an opt-in flag, no transport service for HTTPS POST, no batching scheduler, no retry-with-backoff, no privacy-notice surface, no anonymized-aggregate compute pipeline. T5.D8 ships the product-side schema + emitter shim that consumes Foundations transport; T5.D9 consumes the aggregated feed in the Admin Dashboard. Both remain in degraded-shim mode until Foundations lands the wire.
- **Performance budgets.** **No documented budget anywhere.** `grep -rn "bundle.*budget\|max.*size\|webpack.*performance" src config` returns 0 hits in shipped configs. Current production bundle sizes (`ls -la release/assets/sp-search-*-web-part.js | sort -k5 -n -r`): `sp-search-filters-web-part.js` **14.75 MB**, `sp-search-results-web-part.js` **14.50 MB**, `sp-search-admin-manager-web-part.js` **11.12 MB**, `sp-search-manager-web-part.js` **11.12 MB**, `sp-search-box-web-part.js` **8.49 MB**, `sp-search-verticals-web-part.js` **7.96 MB**. The combined per-page payload for a typical Box + Results + Filters + Verticals page is ~46 MB unminified before SPFx's lazy-chunk machinery kicks in (lazy chunks add another `chunk.vendors-*-fluentui-Dialog-*.js` 7.10 MB, `chunk.vendors-*-devextreme-react_core-*.js` 3.53 MB, `chunk.xlsx_xlsx_mjs.js` 2.50 MB on demand). SPFx publishes informal guidance of 1–2 MB per web part for "good citizen" tenants; the smallest SP Search bundle (Verticals at 7.96 MB) is **~4× over** that informal guidance and the Results bundle is **~7× over**. No CI breach gate. `npm run stats` and `npm run stats:json` scripts exist (`package.json:24,25` invoke `heft build --clean --production --emit-stats`) but no enforcement; the `webpack-bundle-analyzer` devDep (`package.json:79`) is configured for opt-in inspection only.
- **`webApiPermissionRequests` not declared.** `grep -rn "webApiPermissionRequests" config` returns 0 hits in `config/package-solution.json` despite `docs/admin-guide.md:240-242` documenting that the Graph People vertical requires `People.Read`. The SharePoint admin center API access page has nothing to approve — admins must add the permission request manually after install. Journey A Step 1 [Polish] flags it.

Closed/Changed-Form items already in Foundations' surface (per Appendix A): BUG-004 (XSS via `newPageUrl` Closed), SEC-003 (collection name length-validated Closed), SEC-005 (Teams URL sovereign-cloud Closed), A11Y-001 (KQL `aria-expanded` Closed), A11Y-002 (`aria-activedescendant` Closed), A11Y-003 (gallery `aria-label` Closed), A11Y-006 (suggestion remove keyboard shortcut Closed). Still-Open items in Foundations' path: A11Y-004 (mode toggle fieldset/legend), A11Y-005 (scope selector `aria-describedby`), SEC-004 (saved-search JSON schema validation — owned by T2.D3 implementation; Foundations Appendix-A tag), SEC-002 Changed-Form (`allow-scripts` retained for WOPI — documented WONTFIX), ARCH-002 (formatter implementation split between store and web part), ARCH-003 (initialization order dependency not enforced — multi-context aspect handed to T3.D10).

#### Gap to "amazing"

The audience profile is "any SPFx-capable tenant, self-serve, no SI hand-holding" — and Foundations is the surface that decides whether `git clone && npm install && npm run package` produces a `.sppkg` an admin can deploy. Today five gaps stop that promise. **First, the documented build path doesn't run.** `npm run package` halts at lint because of a single-line ordering bug in `pnpPropertyControlsFix.ts`; `npm run type-check` invokes a non-existent Heft flag; the deployment guide still tells admins to run `gulp bundle --ship` after the 1.22 migration removed gulpfile.js. Three different commands fail or mislead before any code is even built. **Second, the SPFx 1.22 / Heft migration sits on an unmerged 91-commit branch** with no merge criteria and no release tag, so admins who follow the docs from `main` get the prior 1.21 + gulp chain, admins who clone the feature branch get the un-shipped Heft path, and neither is "the version we ship." **Third, the bundle is enormous and no one is watching.** Per-web-part bundles range 7.96–14.75 MB before lazy chunks; a typical four-web-part page is ~46 MB unminified. SPFx informal guidance is 1–2 MB. There is no documented budget, no CI breach gate, no per-web-part size attribution in any artifact admins or developers see, and no enforcement against regression as new Adopt-class spfx-toolkit components (Comments at T2.D4, ManageAccess at T2.D5) land. **Fourth, the release engineering surface is empty.** No `.github/workflows/`, no `CHANGELOG.md`, no semver tags, no GitHub Releases entry, no `.sppkg` artifact pinned anywhere admins can download, no PR template, no Dependabot. The "self-serve any tenant" launch profile cannot ship without at least a CI-built `.sppkg` released against a tagged commit. **Fifth, accessibility ships without a baseline.** The audit closed four of six March 22 a11y items but two remain open, no axe-core / Lighthouse gate runs in CI, no `prefers-reduced-motion` respect anywhere in source, no `FocusTrapZone` on the panels T1.D1 and T1.D6 are about to add, and no published WCAG 2.1 AA conformance statement — the kind of artifact an enterprise procurement review asks for in the first 30 minutes. Telemetry plumbing and the docs sweep are real but lower-stakes shaped versions of the same pattern: each ships nothing, and each is the prerequisite for a downstream T-track deliverable that is otherwise blocked. Foundations is the cheapest track to fix and the most expensive track to defer — every other track is downstream of one or more of these gaps.

#### Deliverables

1. **Fix `pnpPropertyControlsFix.ts` lint blocker so `npm run package` produces `.sppkg`**
   - **Description:** Reorder declarations in `src/styles/pnpPropertyControlsFix.ts` so the `PNP_COLLECTION_DATA_CSS` constant (currently declared at `:42`) is declared above its first use at `:33` (`style.textContent = PNP_COLLECTION_DATA_CSS;`). Two valid shapes: (a) move the `const PNP_COLLECTION_DATA_CSS = `...`;` block to the top of the file above `ensurePnpPropertyControlStyles()`; or (b) keep the order and disable the rule for the file with a top-of-file `/* eslint-disable @typescript-eslint/no-use-before-define */` comment justified by the inline JSDoc explaining the hoisting rationale. Prefer (a) — mechanical reorder, no rule suppression. Verify by running `npm run package` end-to-end and confirming a `.sppkg` lands at `sharepoint/solution/sp-search.sppkg` per `config/package-solution.json:38`. Add a one-line guard test to `tests/utils/configValidation.test.ts` (or new `tests/styles/pnpPropertyControlsFix.test.ts`) that imports the module — TypeScript compilation alone catches a future re-introduction of the same ordering. Pre-captured Phase 0.2 verification finding F-1.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (d) "would prevent install / build". `npm run package` halts at the ESLint stage before TypeScript or Webpack runs, so no `.sppkg` is produced through documented commands. The audience-profile rule "self-serve any tenant" requires that `git clone && npm install && npm run package` produces a deployable artifact. Today it does not. SARIF evidence captured at `release/analysis-logs/lint.sarif` documents the failure for downstream verification.
   - **Effort:** S
   - **Priority:** P0
   - **Depends on:** none
   - **Source:** Phase 0.2 verification finding F-1; Journey A Step 1 [Blocker]; Phase 7 discovery: `release/analysis-logs/lint.sarif` `"level": "error"`, `"text": "'PNP_COLLECTION_DATA_CSS' was used before it was defined."`
   - **Acceptance signal:** Running `npm run package` from a clean checkout completes without lint errors and produces `sharepoint/solution/sp-search.sppkg`. ESLint reports zero `@typescript-eslint/no-use-before-define` violations against `src/styles/pnpPropertyControlsFix.ts`. SARIF output regenerated at `release/analysis-logs/lint.sarif` shows zero error-level entries.

3. **Fix `npm run type-check` script (`heft build --clean --lite` → working invocation)**
   - **Description:** Replace `package.json:28` `"type-check": "heft build --clean --lite"` with a working invocation. Two valid shapes: (a) `"type-check": "tsc --noEmit -p tsconfig.json"` — direct TypeScript invocation that bypasses Heft entirely (the fallback Phase 0.2 verification confirmed passes); or (b) `"type-check": "heft build --clean --typescript-only"` if the Heft 1.2.x pipeline supports a typecheck-only task (verify against `@rushstack/heft` documentation before committing — current evidence is that `--lite` is not recognized). Prefer (a) for self-contained semantics — the script does what its name says without depending on Heft pipeline knowledge. Update `docs/deployment-guide.md:18` and any other doc reference to reflect the chosen command. Add the script to the D2 pre-merge regression suite. Pre-captured Phase 0.2 verification finding F-2.
   - **Why it matters:** Ties to (e) Journey A Step 1 [Blocker]. The deployment guide tells admins to run `npm run type-check` before packaging; today the script fails or no-ops without exercising the type checker. The fallback `npx tsc --noEmit` passes (so the type system is clean), but the misleading wrapper means admins either skip the step or report a phantom failure. P1 (not P0) because the workaround "run `tsc --noEmit` directly" is one command away.
   - **Effort:** S
   - **Priority:** P1
   - **Depends on:** none
   - **Source:** Phase 0.2 verification finding F-2; Journey A Step 1 [Blocker]; Phase 7 discovery: `package.json:28` `"type-check": "heft build --clean --lite"`; `--lite` is not recognized by Heft 1.2.7 (`devDependencies."@rushstack/heft": "^1.2.7"` per `package.json:73`)
